  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e56d3468-ec1d-417d-9254-b4a4542770a1'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/566923137" />
    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9514316-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363844368p2/9514316.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/566923137?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie" href="/user/show/9514316-maggie">Maggie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer566923137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer794358141352329193">This book was given to me by relatives as a random stocking stuffer when I was a pre-teen. I never expected to like it, but as soon as I started reading, it became my favorite book, and remained my favorite book for years afterward. I read this book cover to cover at least 15 times as a teen (I'm actually underexaggerating), and never once made it to the end without bawling my eyes out. It's still sitting on my shelf, over a decade later, falling apart at the seams from all the use it got in my </span>
  <span id="freeText794358141352329193" style="display:none">This book was given to me by relatives as a random stocking stuffer when I was a pre-teen. I never expected to like it, but as soon as I started reading, it became my favorite book, and remained my favorite book for years afterward. I read this book cover to cover at least 15 times as a teen (I'm actually underexaggerating), and never once made it to the end without bawling my eyes out. It's still sitting on my shelf, over a decade later, falling apart at the seams from all the use it got in my younger years. I haven't read it since, but I just saw someone mention McDaniel on another review, and felt inclined to post a comment about it here. I'm grateful for the throwback.<br /><br />I tried reading other Lurlene McDaniel books in younger years, but none of them got to me like this one. This book is AMAZING, and I'm so glad I was reminded of it today. It's a beautiful story of love, loss, and everything in between. I can only hope I find a love one day that's half as special as the love the protagonists in this story had for each other.<br /><br />If I remember correctly, McDaniel apparently lost a child to a terminal illness (or something along those lines), so it doesn't surprise me that she knew how to bring the love and pain of this story forward in such a real and pure way. I can't wait to pass it along as a random stocking stuffer to my future daughter one day! A+++ </span>
  <a data-text-id="794358141352329193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11877990522531056832" style="display:none"><br />“If it's possible to send a message from heaven, I'll get one to you.” -Luke<br /><br />~Spoilers~<br /><br />You want a book that rips out your heart and stomps all over it? You got it with this one! <br /><br />This book is beautiful and the kind of love any woman wants from a man. Childhood friends and still deeply in love with one another. They reach high school and are still going strong, their love never dies. Then Juile finds out Luke has cancer and everything goes downhill. However her love for him never died in fact it grew stronger. She went with him to every doctor's appointments and was there for him when he wasn't strong. She prayed that he would stay alive but the tumor in his lungs grew worse and sadly, Luke died. However the ending his beautiful and Luke sends a message to Juile from heaven, flowers covering the football field. <br /><br />I read this book in class and I cried my eyes out for an hour in front of my class. This book is easy to read and a very short read. So grab a copy and begin to read. But have tissues with you!<br /> </span>

<div id="review_83909835" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83909835" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83909835?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83909835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17629728563973213867">Don't Die My Love by Lurlene McDaniel is a beautiful love story that will pull at your heartstrings. I read it in one sitting and fell for the main characters right away. Luke and Julie's love for each other was truly genuine IMHO, and I was sad for Luke when he was diagnosed with Hodgkin's. The events unfolded at a steady pace, but I was not prepared for the final outcome, or rather in denial I should say. As realistic as it was, I was still hoping against hope and eventually found myself reach</span>
  <span id="freeText17629728563973213867" style="display:none">Don't Die My Love by Lurlene McDaniel is a beautiful love story that will pull at your heartstrings. I read it in one sitting and fell for the main characters right away. Luke and Julie's love for each other was truly genuine IMHO, and I was sad for Luke when he was diagnosed with Hodgkin's. The events unfolded at a steady pace, but I was not prepared for the final outcome, or rather in denial I should say. As realistic as it was, I was still hoping against hope and eventually found myself reaching for the tissues, which is saying a lot as I usually don't get emotionally vested in fictional stories.<br /><br />About the story… Luke has loved Julie since he was a little boy. When the story commences, they are high school sweethearts and Luke, who comes from poor means, has worked hard to become the star football player with good grades in the hopes of getting into college with a scholarship and making something of himself. He loves Julie with all his heart and she feels the same for him. Their lives are turned upside down when Luke is diagnosed with Hodgkin's, which is a form of cancer. He fights for his life and struggles to gain his stamina back after a bout of chemo and radiation. Luke is definitely the perfect model of a great guy. He is loving, thoughtful, strong and courageous. His comeback gives the reader hope, but hang on as the ride takes turns and twists your mind and your heart will struggle against. <br /><br />This story really had me on an emotional roll-a-coaster. It was angsty, happy, sad, but most of all beautiful. I highly recommend it if you want to read about genuine love. Great story!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17629728563973213867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3853367388850954713">The author, Lurlene McDaniel, does an awesome job in her work. I wish I had more time to read her books. I love to read her writing. It is so vivid. I can actually put myself in the main characters place. <br/><br/>This book is an amazing love story. I love how the main character shows how devoted to her boyfriend.   <span id="freeText3853367388850954713" style="display:none">The author, Lurlene McDaniel, does an awesome job in her work. I wish I had more time to read her books. I love to read her writing. It is so vivid. I can actually put myself in the main characters place. <br /><br />This book is an amazing love story. I love how the main character shows how devoted to her boyfriend. Yet, as many changes he faces she stills stands by his side even when he doesn’t want her love. Don’t Die, My Love takes you a journey of two young adults as there undivided attention to one another and the choices each person makes will send your mind on an expedition on what true love really is. And the struggles that come with it. My heart broke the some of the problems they faced. I even cried once or twice. <br /><br />Lurlene adds turns and twists. I wasn’t able to put the book down. I like how the author always incorporates at least one person that has cancer. Her son had cancer so that is one thing that you can find in every one of her books. She does an awesome job on the way she writes her books. I have read many of her books and wish to read more. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2931742267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2931742267" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2931742267?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=medical">medical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2931742267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8197477638222149040">Adapted in the 1990's into the Lifetime "Moment of Truth" film <i>Shattered Hearts</i>, this novel, which follows two high school sweethearts trying to cope when one is diagnosed with a serious illness, is still as timely and relevant today as ever, although perhaps a bit less likely than it was in the 1990's. Not only does <i>Don't Die, My Love</i> look at the harrowing nature of an illness through the eyes of a young person, but it also on the side looks at the difficult transition from high school to colle</span>
  <span id="freeText8197477638222149040" style="display:none">Adapted in the 1990's into the Lifetime "Moment of Truth" film <i>Shattered Hearts</i>, this novel, which follows two high school sweethearts trying to cope when one is diagnosed with a serious illness, is still as timely and relevant today as ever, although perhaps a bit less likely than it was in the 1990's. Not only does <i>Don't Die, My Love</i> look at the harrowing nature of an illness through the eyes of a young person, but it also on the side looks at the difficult transition from high school to college, and how hard it can be to know what you really want to do with the rest of your life at that age.<br /><br />Albeit a little preachy at times and somewhat predictable, <i>Don't Die, My Love</i> is a very powerful novel and it presents very realistic characters. McDaniel really understands grief though a younger person's eyes, as well as the general attitude and mentality of high schoolers, which gives the book a very realistic tone that many other books in this sort of genre can't pull off as effectively.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8197477638222149040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13606210352685583642" style="display:none">Want to see more bookish things from me? Check out my Youtube channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCferU-BCL2dlFjWdD0rS75Q/videos">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCfer...</a><br /><br />2.5/5 Stars <br /><br />Luke has always loved Julie since he was a child even though Julie originally hadn't felt the same way. Now, years later, Julie and Luke have been highschool sweethearts for 3 years. They plan on attending college together where Luke will play football and eventually marrying. When Luke receives a scary diagnosis, Julie decides to stand by him and show him how much she loves him. <br /><br />The book is heart breakingly sad. It's an extremely fast read which I finished in 3 hours. It's an honest portrayal of a situation like the one told in this book. Luke is adorable and I wish I had a boy who cared that much about me. I loved the ending and the thing that Luke did for Julie (I won't say what because spoilers but OMG MY HEART). I didn't like Julie in particular and at times found her to be rather annoying. Julie's mother made me very angry and annoyed about how she was constantly on Julie's case about college, although I do understand her reasoning behind it. I also didn't care for a lot of the dialogue in the book. It seemed a bit slow at times but over all, it was a touching story. </span>

<div id="review_139944399" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139944399" />
    <a title="Kendra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4362534-kendra"><img alt="Kendra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285946417p2/4362534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139944399?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kendra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kendra" href="/user/show/4362534-kendra">Kendra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4362534-kendra?shelf=finished-irp-books">finished-irp-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139944399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16466429553056530380">	Don’t Die, My Love is a book about growing up, love the same person you grew up hating, and have to go through knowing the person you love has only a short life to live. Julie Ellis is a young girl who is dating the perfect boy that every girl in the school would be lucky to date, but the only problem is that he doesn’t care much for her an only has his mind on making into the big times for football. Luke Mulden is her love, he has liked Julie since they were little but she was so mean to him. </span>
  <span id="freeText16466429553056530380" style="display:none">	Don’t Die, My Love is a book about growing up, love the same person you grew up hating, and have to go through knowing the person you love has only a short life to live. Julie Ellis is a young girl who is dating the perfect boy that every girl in the school would be lucky to date, but the only problem is that he doesn’t care much for her an only has his mind on making into the big times for football. Luke Mulden is her love, he has liked Julie since they were little but she was so mean to him. Luke was the quarter back for his high school football team, and his dreams mean more to him then anything. Luke was sick for very long, Julie had no idea what was wrong but Luke wanted to finish the football season. Once he finally decided to go to the doctors he finds out that he has cancer. He loses all his hair, he doesn’t eat, he gets sick all the time and through all of this Julie didn’t leave his side. Julie and him travel to California for the summer to visit with Luke’s uncle. When they come they come to find out that he has a tumor in his lung. Julie and him talk about getting married and Luke doesn’t know what to tell her. He ends up having to go through a big surgery he knows that this surgery could take his life but Julie has all confident that everything will be fixed. Julie, Luke’s mom and Julie’s family wait for the news of how Luke’s surgery goes.<br />	This book has a very good begin, it’s sad, makes you want to fall in love and it will make you cry. I love the author made it so Julie’s story about her life seemed like it was a true story. This book made be think of what if this happened to me and my boyfriend which made me for sad. The story of the love in California made me really happy and be very thankful for what relationship I am in! This book is trying to get a point across that you should always live your life on the edge, and always remember that life is short. This story really brings out that when you really love someone that you need to stay by their side through anything. <br />	I give this book 5 stars because I think any girl who loves a good love story they would like this book a lot. It’s definitely a romance book which isn’t for everyone so if your into those books like Dear John I wouldn’t read this book. If you really like heart warming stories and cute young relationships I would recommend this book for you.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16466429553056530380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9598930842844612272"> <u> Don't Die my Love</u> is the saddest love story i have ever read in my life. It talks about this guy who is a really good football player, but one day his girlfriend notices something wrong with him and suggest that he sees a doctor.   <span id="freeText9598930842844612272" style="display:none"> <u> Don't Die my Love</u> is the saddest love story i have ever read in my life. It talks about this guy who is a really good football player, but one day his girlfriend notices something wrong with him and suggest that he sees a doctor. He was afraid to go to the doctor because he's scared that if something was wrong with him that he won't be able to play football anymore, and football was basically his future. When he finally went to the doctors with the encouragement of his girlfriend, the doctor told him he had leukemia. That's when everything started to change. This book will leave you will and endless stream of tears falling down your eyes.<br /> I would recommend this book to anyone who loves a sad story, because this might probably one of the saddest stories you will ever read. It is such a touching book you have no idea what it can do to you. I would also recommend this book to people who want to see how deep you are because if you feel you won't cry over something sad, you definitely will after reading this story.</span>

I can't even get myself together or stop the tears from falling...<br />Luke and Julie's love story is heartbreakingly beautiful. It, once more, showed that true love can go through anything even deadly diseases. Every single word of this book touched my heart. Every single paragraph made me crave for more and the end, oh well, the end made me end up sobbing and sobbing for very long minutes.<br /><br />“And If I can’t wait for you at the end of an aisle on our wedding day, I’ll wait for you in heaven.”<br /><br />“If it’s possible to send a message from heaven, I’ll get one to you.”<br /><br />I can't make a better review because my heart is too broken. After this book, after feeling so heartbroken by its imense beauty, I don't think I will be able to see love the same way. It's so hard to explain my feelings right now, I feel like I could cry for days because of this.<br /><br />Just hearbreakingly perfect...</span>
  <a data-text-id="537032094397413578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2029685986" />
    <a title="Gracie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68619504-gracie"><img alt="Gracie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596067616p2/68619504.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer14614368548701047648">Don't Die, My Love<br/>Lurlene McDaniel<br/>250 pp. New York, NY.<br/>Random House Children's Book. $5.50<br/>ISBN: 0-553-56715-2<br/><br/>	Everyone loves a good cry, and no one delivers heart wrenching stories better than Lurlene McDaniel.   <span id="freeText14614368548701047648" style="display:none">Don't Die, My Love<br />Lurlene McDaniel<br />250 pp. New York, NY.<br />Random House Children's Book. $5.50<br />ISBN: 0-553-56715-2<br /><br />	Everyone loves a good cry, and no one delivers heart wrenching stories better than Lurlene McDaniel. Don't Die, My Love by Lurlene McDaniel is a beautiful story of young heart breaking, tragic romance! This book was burning in past times when young love was the center of attention and still is! The story truly shows strong and passionate relationship between two teens and struggles on health, love, and even putting up with pushy parents. It makes you feel a relationship was match made in heaven. People who's looking for forbidden love presented a breathtaking couple, then this book is definitely the book for you!<br />	Julie Ellis and Luke Muldenhower—a football star—have been "engaged" since sixth grade. This attractive high-school couple were perfect together and had everything set good for them: popularity, good grades, and love. Unfortunately Luke develops Hodgkin's Lymphoma...Julie is determined to help him through his chemotherapy and get through this ordeal so their lives can return to normal. But Luke ended pushing Julie away because he knows clearly that he is faced with a life-threatening illness, not a simple cold or flu. With the pressure of high school and Luke's health, they wonder if their love can make it through.<br />	 Don't Die, My Love has written many novels but this one is my favorite. Furthermore it's the first book that I couldn't put down until it was finish. See how powerful and inspirational her books are? While reading I feel so warm inside and I'll admit that I cried. You'll too because their love life is so heart warming and tragic. Nevertheless, it's so beautiful! But the question is, can love hold a couple together through their most difficult times? It's up to you to see the answer yourself. What are you still waiting for, hurry and get a copy. By the way, before you start reading, have the tissues by your side. If not you'll get you pillow wet...</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214671644" />
    <a title="Jordyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6219932-jordyn"><img alt="Jordyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437892437p2/6219932.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214671644?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jordyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jordyn" href="/user/show/6219932-jordyn">Jordyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6219932-jordyn?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214671644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4064997365460377004">This was my first time reading an actual romance novel--I've read books with love stories at their core, obviously, but I've never read one of these sappy romances. <i> Don't Die, My Love</i> actually wasn't that painful to read, though. I got pretty bored when Julie and Luke are on vacation in California, but I liked the rest of the book pretty well. I was trying to figure out why books like this would be important for teen readers, and I actually think that some teens could learn some things from the</span>
  <span id="freeText4064997365460377004" style="display:none">This was my first time reading an actual romance novel--I've read books with love stories at their core, obviously, but I've never read one of these sappy romances. <i> Don't Die, My Love</i> actually wasn't that painful to read, though. I got pretty bored when Julie and Luke are on vacation in California, but I liked the rest of the book pretty well. I was trying to figure out why books like this would be important for teen readers, and I actually think that some teens could learn some things from them: firstly, I know that death is a daunting topic for everyone, regardless of age, so reading about illness and death happening to young people would help young readers know that they're not alone. Also, I thought that the whole Julie-only-wanting-to-follow-Luke-and-not-worry-about-her-independent-future thread was very important for teen girls because I know that so many girls don't think they have an identity outside of their boyfriends, and they blindly follow them to whatever college, but what do they do when that boyfriend is out of the picture for whatever reason? Basically, this book wasn't my favorite, but I can see why we would be assigned it for this class.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4064997365460377004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2674840393?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hailey Wheaton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hailey Wheaton" href="/user/show/71562949-hailey-wheaton">Hailey Wheaton</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9634581555839024244">Personal Response:<br/>I thought that this book was actually pretty good. I didn’t think I would like it because the title of it is very cheesy, but it was very good. I liked how Julie had a connection with Luke’s family and how Luke had a connection with Julie’s family. <br/><br/><br/>Plot summary:<br/>In the book <i>Don’t Die, My Love</i> Luke and Julie are two high school students that are in love, and plan on living the rest of their life. Throughout their high school years, everything seemed to be perfect. Suddenly Julie </span>
  <span id="freeText9634581555839024244" style="display:none">Personal Response:<br />I thought that this book was actually pretty good. I didn’t think I would like it because the title of it is very cheesy, but it was very good. I liked how Julie had a connection with Luke’s family and how Luke had a connection with Julie’s family. <br /><br /><br />Plot summary:<br />In the book <i>Don’t Die, My Love</i> Luke and Julie are two high school students that are in love, and plan on living the rest of their life. Throughout their high school years, everything seemed to be perfect. Suddenly Julie noticed that Luke seemed to be very sick. Luke went into the doctor and found out that he has Hodgkin Lymphoma. He finds out that he needs to go through chemotherapy, so he did but it didn't work. He then had to go through radiation to try to totally treat his cancer. The doctors believe that he is better and they allow him to go to Los Angeles with Julie to his uncles' wedding. After they return from the very well spent trip he is supposed to go to a checkup with the doctors, but he skipped it so he could play his senior year of football. There was nothing that seemed to be wrong with Luke until he passed out in one of his games and was immediately rushed to the hospital to get checked up on. The doctors found a tumor by his heart and lung, the doctors knew that it needed to be taken out because otherwise, he would surely die. They were into the procedure when they realized that the tumor was actually on his heart and later on he passes away. Julie was absolutely devasted to the point where she was depressed and felt nothing could help her move on. Until one day she had discovered that Luke had planted bulbs in the football field before he passed away that said I love you.<br /><br /><br />Characterization:<br />Julie started out as the happiest girl on Earth and nothing could change that until Luke became sick. Luke was also always happy as long as Julie was happy. Luke always tried to keep the most positive mid-set as possible even though he knew that times would get tough. Julie was very depressed and lonely at the end of the book when Luke died until she realized that she was left a secret love surprise and then became very happy.<br /><br />Recommendations:<br />I would 100 percent recommend this to the high school level because the book does go into great detail at times. I would also recommend this book to anyone that has been in love and lost their significant other, just to help them realize that they are not alone. This would also be a great book for a quick read because you can get hooked on it very easily and not want to put it down, even though it is a more lengthy book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9634581555839024244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1554314892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1554314892" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13012187-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348185636p2/13012187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1554314892?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/13012187-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13012187-sara?shelf=a-real-eye-roller">a-real-eye-roller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13012187-sara?shelf=unlikeable-protag">unlikeable-protag</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1554314892&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1554314892" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3646077188518024019">This wasn't a BAD book, if you like tearjerkers and high school sweethearts. But I found Julie's utter dependency on Luke to be really grating. I mean, I have a HUGE loyalty kink , I ship a number of pairings involving a clingy partner who puts their lover on a pedestal. But Julie basically had no life outside of her boyfriend. She didn't care where she went to college as long as it was with him, she insisted on going to every doctor's appointment, staying with him during chemo and radiation, sh</span>
  <span id="freeText3646077188518024019" style="display:none">This wasn't a BAD book, if you like tearjerkers and high school sweethearts. But I found Julie's utter dependency on Luke to be really grating. I mean, I have a HUGE loyalty kink , I ship a number of pairings involving a clingy partner who puts their lover on a pedestal. But Julie basically had no life outside of her boyfriend. She didn't care where she went to college as long as it was with him, she insisted on going to every doctor's appointment, staying with him during chemo and radiation, she clung to him like a leech. She flat-out said several times that her life was worth NOTHING without this guy and she completely shut down when he died.<br /><br />Now, to be fair, Luke had cancer and that's a big deal. I can get Julie wanting to spend every moment she could with him...but she also firmly insisted that he wasn't dying. That he'd beat his cancer and they'd have their whole future ahead of him. Even when he was making peace with the fact that he might not survive in the end, she kept trying to shut him down. I get it, denial's powerful when death is happening, but Julie took it to really uncomfortable extremes. Luke basically said he felt PRESSURED by her to get well, to put his cancer behind him once he was in remission and she still kept insisting YOU WILL LIVE, LUKE, YOU WILL LIIIIIVE.<br /><br />Normally I'd find a pushy mother like Julie's annoying, especially when she went on and on about what SHE wanted for her daughter and how important it was to HER that she go to college and be a success. But in this case, she had a point about the girl lacking direction. Luke himself even called her on her dependent behavior, but at the same time he was an enabler.<br /><br />Losing someone you love is tough shit and you don't just get over it. Believe me, I know. But Julie's handling of the situation went beyond understandable and into really cringeworthy territory. I couldn't even enjoy the ending even though the premise was kind of sweet.<br /><br />SIDE NOTES:<br />I thought I would hate Julie's father for being sexist in the beginning, but he turned out to be...not that bad. He clearly cared about Luke as a person and not just as his star football player.<br /><br />Solena annoyed me at first, with her weeping because her boyfriend TALKED TO ANOTHER GIRL OH NOES, but when Julie's clinginess kicked in full-throttle I shrugged Solena off as just being an irrational teenager. At least she and Frank were normal in comparison.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3646077188518024019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1388239351" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1388239351" />
    <a title="Madison Florea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44653200-madison-florea"><img alt="Madison Florea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555427160p2/44653200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1388239351?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madison Florea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madison Florea" href="/user/show/44653200-madison-florea">Madison Florea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1388239351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6557582013943792755">“If it's possible to send a message from heaven, I'll get one to you.”<br/><br/>I read this book when I was younger and didn't fully appreciate it until now. P.s. one of the reasons I read it when I was younger was because I had (okay, have) a crush on the male model on the cover. This is a heart wrenching tale of love, loss and true soulmates. If you aren't in tears by the end of this book, I don't even know what to say. I had to stop reading multiple times just to get through the last few chapters. I kn</span>
  <span id="freeText6557582013943792755" style="display:none">“If it's possible to send a message from heaven, I'll get one to you.”<br /><br />I read this book when I was younger and didn't fully appreciate it until now. P.s. one of the reasons I read it when I was younger was because I had (okay, have) a crush on the male model on the cover. This is a heart wrenching tale of love, loss and true soulmates. If you aren't in tears by the end of this book, I don't even know what to say. I had to stop reading multiple times just to get through the last few chapters. I know what you're thinking, who wants to read a book that makes them cry? But it is so much more than that. The author, Lurlene McDaniel delves into what it's like to find true love at a young age and the sacrifices couples will make to ensure the relationships survival, no matter the obstacles. <br /><br />Luke and Julie are two high school students in love, Luke is a rising football star and Julie is the football coaches son. Is it just me or is every Luke in history attractive and romantic? ANYWAYS, Luke doesn't have the best living or financial situation. His father died from a warehouse accident and his mother has been doing her best to support her only son. Julie on the other hand has both parents and lives in a well off neighborhood. Luke had been in love with Julie since sixth grade and when puberty kicked in, Julie fell for Luke. At fourteen Luke showed up at Julie's door with a bouquet of flowers, the secret to Julie's heart ever since. “I'll cover you in flowers someday, Julie-girl.” <br /><br />The two are your average couple living in a small town, double dates with friends, football games on the weekends. Until one day, Julie discovers a lump on Luke's neck. She pleads with him to go to the doctor, he's stubborn because he doesn't want to worry his mother with money and believes it to be the common flu. When he finally makes his way to the doctors office, the worst is revealed. Luke has a rare form of cancer and needs to begin chemo immediately.<br /><br />This book has ups, it certainly has downs and everything else in between. This is a story of growing up and learning to deal with what life has to offer. “Nobody gets to pick what life gives them” <br /><br />This book is truly for anyone. Theres no sex scenes, no graphic hospital descriptions. This is a true classic and a quick and entertaining read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6557582013943792755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1012737671" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1012737671" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33281417-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593821843p2/33281417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1012737671?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/33281417-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1012737671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8814049104169365679">I'm warning you now, there are spoilers in this review. <br/><br/>I love the fact that Lurlene McDaniel writes books that deal with real life issues that people experience everyday. I applaud her for tackling that challenge and succeeding. I do enjoy some of her books. I love how at the end of the book, Julie sees the flowers that Luke planted for her on the football field knowing he had to have planted them months in advance or else they wouldn't have bloomed. That goes without saying that he knew he was</span>
  <span id="freeText8814049104169365679" style="display:none">I'm warning you now, there are spoilers in this review. <br /><br />I love the fact that Lurlene McDaniel writes books that deal with real life issues that people experience everyday. I applaud her for tackling that challenge and succeeding. I do enjoy some of her books. I love how at the end of the book, Julie sees the flowers that Luke planted for her on the football field knowing he had to have planted them months in advance or else they wouldn't have bloomed. That goes without saying that he knew he was going to die. <br /><br />I did enjoy this book simply for the fact that it deals with struggles that occur in reality as opposed to books like Divergent and The Hunger Games, both fantastic books but based strictly in fantasy worlds.<br /><br />Although I enjoyed this book, thinking about the fact that he dies at the end, as I write this, brings tears to my eyes and I haven't read it since I was 14 years old and that was seven years ago. I still can't get over the fact that he died and that's why I gave it the rating that I did. <br /><br />This book reminds me of The Fault in Our Stars, another novel that deals with teenage cancer patients. The comfort that I find in The Fault in Our Stars, as morbid as it may sound, is that you know eventually that Hazel will join Gus in the afterlife, whatever that is for them, relatively soon. Again, I may sound morbid, but that thought is what makes me enjoy The Fault in Our Stars a little more than Don't Die, My Love.<br /><br />I try to find the positive in sad books that I read and knowing that Hazel is just as sick as Gus was makes me think that she will join him soon and be with him again. Julie is a perfectly healthy 18 year-old high school senior with her entire life ahead of her. The idea that she no longer has the person she thought she was going to spend the rest of her life with by her side makes me terribly sad. <br /><br />Lurlene McDaniel is a fantastic author but I'm a sucker for happy endings and this one didn't do that for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8814049104169365679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m25hE46Co3D0BPhq+dYK/PLk2YKST5eEixxiFLiJKI7XjOkyVHExSP/F6QsPGgwjqyYnbJH2ju+QDmPQWvJ1Aw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/Fkf8tk+Jq7xwh03xoUE81B/aQZUOIKSJak2AP33nrSwu5fTA820lvoDDFYwSQIsCb2X6FeBm/k+uzfEH4zDOQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer17789014298197936016">Lurlene McDaniel (born c. 1948) is an author who has written over 50 young adult books. She is well known for writing about characters struggling with chronic and terminal illnesses, such as cancer, diabetes, and organ failure.<br/><br/><br/>Other places to find her are...<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.facebook.com/lurlenemcdaniel/'>https://www.facebook.com/lurlenemcdan...</a><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.penguinrandomhouse.com/authors/19817/lurlene-mcdaniel'>http://www.penguinrandomhouse.com/aut...</a><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.youtube.com/user/LurleneMc'>http://www.youtube.com/user/LurleneMc</a></span>
  <span id="freeText17789014298197936016" style="display:none">Lurlene McDaniel (born c. 1948) is an author who has written over 50 young adult books.
